Rendezvous hash-based routing and shard assignment.\n\nuse crate::topology::{Group, NodeId, Topology};\nuse std::hash::{Hash, Hasher};\nuse twox_hash::XxHash64;\n\n/// Compute a rendezvous score for a shard+node pair.\n///\n/// Higher scores win; used for deterministic shard assignment.\npub fn score(shard_id: u32, node_id: &str) -> u64 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    shard_id.hash(&mut h);\n    node_id.hash(&mut h);\n    h.finish()\n}\n\n/// Assign a shard to `rf` nodes within a single replica group.\n///\n/// `group_nodes` is the subset of nodes belonging to that group.\npub fn assign_shard_in_group(shard_id: u32, group_nodes: &[NodeId], rf: usize) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    let mut scored: Vec<(u64, &NodeId)> = group_nodes\n        .iter()\n        .map(|n| (score(shard_id, n.as_str()), n))\n        .collect();\n    scored.sort_unstable_by(|a, b| b.0.cmp(&a.0));\n    scored\n        .into_iter()\n        .take(rf)\n        .map(|(_, n)| n.clone())\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// All write targets for a document: the RF nodes in EACH replica group.\npub fn write_targets(shard_id: u32, topology: &Topology) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    topology\n        .groups()\n        .flat_map(|group| assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), topology.rf()))\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Select the replica group for a query (round-robin by query chosen group.\npub fn covering_set(shard_count: u32, group: &Group, rf: usize, query_seq: u64) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    (0..shard_count)\n        .map(|shard_id| {\n            let replicas = min).\n81\t    pub score_range: f64,\n82\t}\n83\t\n84\t/// Aggregate results across all queries.\n85\t#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n86\tpub struct AggregateResult {\n87\t    /// Mean Kendall Tau across all queries.\n88\t    pub mean_kendall_tau: f64,\n89\t\n90\t    /// Standard deviation of Kendall Tau.\n91\t    pub std_kendall_tau: f64,\n92\t\n93\t    /// Minimum Kendall Tau observed.\n94\t    pub min_kendall_tau: f64,\n95\t\n96\t    /// Maximum Kendall Tau observed.\n97\t    pub max_kendall_tau: f64,\n98\t\n99\t    /// Percentage of queries with τ ≥ 0.95.\n100\t    pub percent_above_threshold: f64,\n101\t\n102\t    /// Mean Jaccard similarity.\n103\t    pub mean_jaccard: f64,\n104\t\n105\t    /// Mean first divergence position.\n106\t    pub mean_first_divergence: usize,\n107\t\n108\t    /// Shard population statistics (CV of document counts).\n109\t    pub shard_pop_cv: f64,\n110\t\n111\t    /// Shard population ratio (max/median).\n112\t    pub shard_pop_ratio: f64,\n113\t}\n114\t\n115\t/// Simulated score comparability test result.\n116\t#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\n117\tpub struct SimResult {\n118\t    pub params: SimParams,\n119\t    pub aggregate: AggregateResult,\n120\t    pub query_results: Vec<QueryResult>,\n121\t    pub shard_doc_counts: Vec<u64>,\n122\t}\n123\t\n124\t/// Run a score comparability simulation.\n125\t///\n126\t/// This models a simplified ranking system where:\n127\t/// - Documents have relevance scores based on term frequency\n128\t/// - Shards compute scores locally using their own document statistics\n129\t/// - A ground-truth single-index uses global statistics\n130\t///\n131\t/// The simulation measures how well the sharded ordering matches the\n132\t/// ground-truth ordering using Kendall Tau correlation.\n133\tpub fn simulate(params: &SimParams) -> SimResult {\n134\t    use rand::rngs::StdRng;\n135\t    use rand::SeedableRng;\n136\t\n137\t    let mut rng = StdRng::seed_from_u64(params.seed);\n138\t\n139\t    // Generate document distribution across shards with specified skew.\n140\t    let shard_doc_counts = generate_skewed_distribution(\n141\t        params.total_docs,\n142\t        params.shard_count,\n143\t        params.skew_factor,\n144\t        &mut rng,\n145\t    );\n146\t\n147\t    // Compute shard population statistics.\n148\t    let total_docs = shard_doc_counts.iter().sum::<u64>() as f64;\n149\t    let mean_docs = total_docs / params.shard_count as f64;\n150\t    let variance = shard_doc_counts\n151\t        .iter()\n152\t        .map(|&c| (c as f64 - mean_docs).powi(2))\n153\t        .sum::<f64>()\n154\t        / params.shard_count as f64;\n155\t    let cv = variance.sqrt() / mean_docs;\n156\t    let median_docs = median(&shard_doc_counts);\n157\t    let max_docs = *shard_doc_counts.iter().max().unwrap_or(&1) as f64;\n158\t    let pop_ratio = max_docs / median_docs;\n159\t\n160\t    // Run queries and collect results.\n161\t    let mut query_results = Vec::with_capacity(params.num_queries);\n162\t\n163\t    for qid in 0..params.num_queries {\n164\t        let result = run_query(qid, params, &shard_doc_counts, &mut rng);\n165\t        query_results.push(result);\n166\t    }\n167\t\n168\t    // Compute aggregate statistics.\n169\t    let taus: Vec<f64> = query_results.iter().map(|r| r.kendall_tau).collect();\n170\t    let mean_tau = mean(&taus);\n171\t    let std_tau = std_dev(&taus, mean_tau);\n172\t    let min_tau = taus.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::min).unwrap_or(0.0);\n173\t    let max_tau = taus.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::max).unwrap_or(0.0);\n174\t    let above_threshold =\n175\t        taus.iter().filter(|&&t| t >= 0.95).count() as f64 / taus.len() as f64 * 100.0;\n176\t\n177\t    let jaccards: Vec<f64> = query_results.iter().map(|r| r.jaccard_similarity).collect();\n178\t    let mean_jaccard = mean(&jaccards);\n179\t\n180\t    let divergences: Vec<usize> = query_results\n181\t        .iter()\n182\t        .map(|r| r.first_divergence_position)\n183\t        .collect();\n184\t    let mean_divergence = mean_usize(&divergences);\n185\t\n186\t    let aggregate = AggregateResult {\n187\t        mean_kendall_tau: mean_tau,\n188\t        std_kendall_tau: std_tau,\n189\t        min_kendall_tau: min_tau,\n190\t        max_kendall_tau: max_tau,\n191\t        percent_above_threshold: above_threshold,\n192\t        mean_jaccard,\n193\t        mean_first_divergence: mean_divergence,\n194\t        shard_pop_cv: cv,\n195\t        shard_pop_ratio: pop_ratio,\n196\t    };\n197\t\n198\t    SimResult {\n199\t        params: params.clone(),\n200\t        aggregate,\n201\t        query_results,\n202\t        shard_doc_counts,\n203\t    }\n204\t}\n205\t\n206\t/// Generate a skewed document distribution across shards.\n207\t///\n208\t/// Uses a Pareto-like distribution to create realistic skew where\n209\t/// a few shards have many more documents than others.\n210\tfn generate_skewed_distribution(\n211\t    total_docs: u64,\n212\t    shard_count: u32,\n213\t    skew_factor: f64,\n214\t    rng: &mut impl rand::Rng,\n215\t) -> Vec<u64> {\n216\t    // Start with uniform weights.\n217\t    let mut weights: Vec<f64> = (0..shard_count).map(|_| 1.0).collect();\n218\t\n219\t    // Apply skew: scale a few shards by the skew factor.\n220\t    // For skew_factor = 100, scale the top 5% of shards.\n221\t    let num_skewed = (shard_count as f64 / 20.0).ceil() as usize; // Top 5%\n222\t    for i in 0..num_skewed.min(weights.len()) {\n223\t        weights[i] *= skew_factor;\n224\t    }\n225\t\n226\t    // Add some randomness to make it more realistic.\n227\t    for w in &mut weights {\n228\t        *w *= rng.gen_range(0.5..1.5);\n229\t    }\n230\t\n231\t    // Normalize weights to sum to total_docs.\n232\t    let weight_sum: f64 = weights.iter().sum();\n233\t    let scale = total_docs as f64 / weight_sum;\n234\t\n235\t    weights\n236\t        .into_iter()\n237\t        .map(|w| (w * scale).max(1.0) as u64) // Ensure at least 1 doc per shard\n238\t        .collect()\n239\t}\n240\t\n241\t/// Run a single query and compare sharded vs ground-truth results.\n242\tfn run_query(\n243\t    query_id: usize,\n244\t    params: &SimParams,\n245\t    shard_doc_counts: &[u64],\n246\t    rng: &mut impl rand::Rng,\n247\t) -> QueryResult {\n248\t    // Simulate a query by generating random relevance scores for documents.\n249\t    // In a real system, scores would be based on term frequency, IDF, etc.\n250\t    // Here we simulate the key effect: smaller shards tend to produce higher\n251\t    // scores for the same documents because their local statistics are different.\n252\t\n253\t    let total_docs = params.total_docs as usize;\n254\t\n255\t    // Generate ground-truth scores (global IDF).\n256\t    // Each document gets a base relevance score + some noise.\n257\t    let mut ground_truth_scores: Vec<(usize, f64)> = (0..total_docs)\n258\t        .map(|doc_id| {\n259\t            let base_relevance = rng.gen::<f64>(); // Simulated term matching\n260\t            let global_idf = 1.0; // Global IDF is uniform\n261\t            let score = base_relevance * global_idf;\n262\t            (doc_id, score)\n263\t        })\n264\t        .collect();\n265\t\n266\t    // Sort by score descending and take top-K.\n267\t    ground_truth_scores.sort_by(|a, b| b.1.partial_cmp(&a.1).unwrap());\n268\t\n269\t    let ground_truth_top: Vec<usize> = ground_truth_scores\n270\t        .iter()\n271\t        .take(params.top_k)\n272\t        .map(|(id, _)| *id)\n273\t        .collect();\n274\t\n275\t    // Generate sharded scores (local IDF per shard).\n276\t    // Key insight: local IDF is computed from shard-specific document counts.\n277\t    // Smaller shards have fewer docs, so their IDF tends to be higher for\n278\t    // the same term, leading to score inflation.\n279\t\n280\t    let mut sharded_scores: Vec<(usize, f64)> = Vec::new();\n281\t\n282\t    for (shard_id, &doc_count) in shard_doc_counts.iter().enumerate() {\n283\t        let shard_id = shard_id as u32;\n284\t        let doc_count_f64 = doc_count as f64;\n285\t        let total_docs_f64 = params.total_docs as f64;\n286\t\n287\t        // Simulate local IDF effect: smaller shards → higher local IDF.\n288\t        // In real BM25, IDF = log((N - df + 0.5) / (df + 0.5)) where N is doc count.\n289\t        // We model this as: local_idf / global_idf ≈ log(N_global) / log(N_shard).\n290\t        let global_idf_factor = (total_docs_f64 + 1.0).ln();\n291\t        let local_idf_factor = (doc_count_f64 + 1.0).ln();\n292\t        let idf_inflation = global_idf_factor / local_idf_factor.max(0.1);\n293\t\n294\t        // Documents on this shard get scores inflated by the local IDF factor.\n295\t        let start_doc = shard_doc_counts[..shard_id as usize].iter().sum::<u64>() as usize;\n296\t        let end_doc = start_doc + doc_count as usize;\n297\t\n298\t        for (doc_id, base_relevance) in ground_truth_scores\n299\t            .iter()\n300\t            .enumerate()\n301\t            .skip(start_doc)\n302\t            .take(end_doc.min(total_docs) - start_doc)\n303\t        {\n304\t            let score = base_relevance.1 * idf_inflation;\n305\t            sharded_scores.push((doc_id, score));\n306\t        }\n307\t    }\n308\t\n309\t    // Sort sharded scores and take top-K.\n310\t    sharded_scores.sort_by(|a, b| b.1.partial_cmp(&a.1).unwrap());\n311\t\n312\t    let sharded_top: Vec<usize> = sharded_scores\n313\t        .iter()\n314\t        .take(params.top_k)\n315\t        .map(|(id, _)| *id)\n316\t        .collect();\n317\t\n318\t    // Compute Kendall Tau between the two orderings.\n319\t    let kendall_tau = kendall_tau(&ground_truth_top, &sharded_top);\n320\t\n321\t    // Compute Jaccard similarity (set overlap, ignoring order).\n322\t    let jaccard = jaccard_similarity(&ground_truth_top, &sharded_top);\n323\t\n324\t    // Find first divergence position.\n325\t    let first_divergence = ground_truth_top\n326\t        .iter()\n327\t        .zip(sharded_top.iter())\n328\t        .position(|(a, b)| a != b)\n329\t        .unwrap_or(params.top_k);\n330\t\n331\t    // Collect per-shard score statistics.\n332\t    let shard_stats =\n333\t        collect_shard_stats(query_id, shard_doc_counts, &sharded_scores, params.top_k);\n334\t\n335\t    QueryResult {\n336\t        query_id,\n337\t        ground_truth_hits: ground_truth_top.len(),\n338\t        sharded_hits: sharded_top.len(),\n339\t        kendall_tau,\n340\t        jaccard_similarity: jaccard,\n341\t        first_divergence_position: first_divergence,\n342\t        shard_score_stats: shard_stats,\n343\t    }\n344\t}\n345\t\n346\t/// Collect score statistics for each shard.\n347\tfn collect_shard_stats(\n348\t    _query_id: usize,\n349\t    shard_doc_counts: &[u64],\n350\t    sharded_scores: &[(usize, f64)],\n351\t    top_k: usize,\n352\t) -> Vec<ShardScoreStats> {\n353\t    let mut stats = Vec::new();\n354\t\n355\t    // Map doc_id back to its shard.\n356\t    for (shard_idx, &doc_count) in shard_doc_counts.iter().enumerate() {\n357\t        let shard_id = shard_idx as u32;\n358\t        let start_doc = shard_doc_counts[..shard_idx].iter().sum::<u64>() as usize;\n359\t        let end_doc = start_doc + doc_count as usize;\n360\t\n361\t        // Find scores from this shard in the top-K results.\n362\t        let shard_hits: Vec<f64> = sharded_scores\n363\t            .iter()\n364\t            .take(top_k)\n365\t            .filter(|(doc_id, _)| *doc_id >= start_doc && *doc_id < end_doc)\n366\t            .map(|(_, score)| *score)\n367\t            .collect();\n368\t\n369\t        if shard_hits.is_empty() {\n370\t            continue;\n371\t        }\n372\t\n373\t        let min_score = shard_hits.iter().fold(f64::INFINITY, |a, &b| a.min(b));\n374\t        let max_score = shard_hits.iter().fold(f64::NEG_INFINITY, |a, &b| a.max(b));\n375\t        let mean_score = shard_hits.iter().sum::<f64>() / shard_hits.len() as f64;\n376\t\n377\t        stats.push(ShardScoreStats {\n378\t            shard_id,\n379\t            doc_count,\n380\t            hit_count: shard_hits.len(),\n381\t            min_score,\n382\t            max_score,\n383\t            mean_score,\n384\t            score_range: max_score - min_score,\n385\t        });\n386\t    }\n387\t\n388\t    stats\n389\t}\n390\t\n391\t/// Compute Kendall Tau correlation between two ranked lists.\n392\t///\n393\t/// Returns a value in [-1, 1] where:\n394\t/// - 1.0 = identical rankings\n395\t/// - 0.0 = no correlation\n396\t/// - -1.0 = completely inverted rankings\n397\t///\n398\t/// Uses the O(n²) algorithm which is fine for small K (typically ≤ 100).\n399\tfn kendall_tau<T: Eq + std::hash::Hash + std::fmt::Debug>(rank1: &[T], rank2: &[T]) -> f64 {\n400\t    if rank1.is_empty() || rank2.is_empty() {\n401\t        return 1.0;\n402\t    }\n403\t\n404\t    // Create position maps.\n405\t    let pos1: std::collections::HashMap<&T, usize> = rank1\n406\t        .iter()\n407\t        .enumerate()\n408\t        .map(|(i, item)| (item, i))\n409\t        .collect();\n410\t    let pos2: std::collections::HashMap<&T, usize> = rank2\n411\t        .iter()\n412\t        .enumerate()\n413\t        .map(|(i, item)| (item, i))\n414\t        .collect();\n415\t\n416\t    // Collect all unique items from both lists.\n417\t    let all_items: std::collections::HashSet<&T> = rank1.iter().chain(rank2.iter()).collect();\n418\t\n419\t    // Count concordant and discordant pairs.\n420\t    let mut concordant = 0;\n421\t    let mut discordant = 0;\n422\t\n423\t    let items: Vec<&T> = all_items.into_iter().collect();\n424\t    for i in 0..items.len() {\n425\t        for j in (i + 1)..items.len() {\n426\t            let a = items[i];\n427\t            let b = items[j];\n428\t\n429\t            let pos1_a = pos1.get(a);\n430\t            let pos1_b = pos1.get(b);\n431\t            let pos2_a = pos2.get(a);\n432\t            let pos2_b = pos2.get(b);\n433\t\n434\t            // A pair is only counted if both items appear in both lists.\n435\t            let (p1a, p1b, p2a, p2b) = match (pos1_a, pos1_b, pos2_a, pos2_b) {\n436\t                (Some(&x), Some(&y), Some(&u), Some(&v)) => (x, y, u, v),\n437\t                _ => continue,\n438\t            };\n439\t\n440\t            if (p1a < p1b && p2a < p2b) || (p1a > p1b && p2a > p2b) {\n441\t                concordant += 1;\n442\t            } else if (p1a < p1b && p2a > p2b) || (p1a > p1b && p2a < p2b) {\n443\t                discordant += 1;\n444\t            }\n445\t        }\n446\t    }\n447\t\n448\t    let total = concordant + discordant;\n449\t    if total == 0 {\n450\t        return 1.0;\n451\t    }\n452\t\n453\t    (concordant - discordant) as f64 / total as f64\n454\t}\n455\t\n456\t/// Compute Jaccard similarity between two sets (ignoring order).\n457\tfn jaccard_similarity<T: Eq + std::hash::Hash>(set1: &[T], set2: &[T]) -> f64 {\n458\t    let set1_hash: std::collections::HashSet<&T> = set1.iter().collect();\n459\t    let set2_hash: std::collections::HashSet<&T> = set2.iter().collect();\n460\t\n461\t    let intersection = set1_hash.intersection(&set2_hash).count();\n462\t    let union = set1_hash.union(&set2_hash).count();\n463\t\n464\t    if union == 0 {\n465\t        return 1.0;\n466\t    }\n467\t\n468\t    intersection as f64 / union as f64\n469\t}\n470\t\n471\t/// Compute mean of a slice of floats.\n472\tfn mean(values: &[f64]) -> f64 {\n473\t    if values.is_empty() {\n474\t        return 0.0;\n475\t    }\n476\t    values.iter().sum::<f64>() / values.len() as f64\n477\t}\n478\t\n479\t/// Compute standard deviation of a slice of floats.\n480\tfn std_dev(values: &[f64], mean_val: f64) -> f64 {\n481\t    if values.len() <= 1 {\n482\t        return 0.0;\n483\t    }\n484\t    let variance =\n485\t        values.iter().map(|v| (v - mean_val).powi(2)).sum::<f64>() / (values.len() - 1) as f64;\n486\t    variance.sqrt()\n487\t}\n488\t\n489\t/// Compute mean of a slice of usize.\n490\tfn mean_usize(values: &[usize]) -> usize {\n491\t    if values.is_empty() {\n492\t        return 0;\n493\t    }\n494\t    values.iter().sum::<usize>() / values.len()\n495\t}\n496\t\n497\t/// Compute median of a slice of u64.\n498\tfn median(values: &[u64]) -> f64 {\n499\t    if values.is_empty() {\n500\t        return 0.0;\n501\t    }\n502\t    let mut sorted = values.to_vec();\n503\t    sorted.sort();\n504\t    let len = sorted.len();\n505\t    if len % 2 == 0 {\n506\t        (sorted[len / 2 - 1] + sorted[len / 2]) as f64 / 2.0\n507\t    } else {\n508\t        sorted[len / 2] as f64\n509\t    }\n510\t}\n511\t\n512\t// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n513\t// Tests\n514\t// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n515\t\n516\t#[cfg(test)]\n517\tmod tests {\n518\t    use super::*;\n519\t\n520\t    #[test]\n521\t    fn test_kendall_tau_identical() {\n522\t        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n523\t        let b = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n524\t        assert!((kendall_tau(&a, &b) - 1.0).abs() < 0.001);\n525\t    }\n526\t\n527\t    #[test]\n528\t    fn test_kendall_tau_reversed() {\n529\t        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n530\t        let b = vec![5, 4, 3, 2, 1];\n531\t        assert!((kendall_tau(&a, &b) - (-1.0)).abs() < 0.001);\n532\t    }\n533\t\n534\t    #[test]\n535\t    fn test_kendall_tau_partial_overlap() {\n536\t        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n537\t        let b = vec![1, 3, 2, 4, 5]; // Only 2 and 3 are swapped\n538\t                                     // One discordant pair (2,3) out of 10 total: tau = (9 - 1) / 10 = 0.8\n539\t        let tau = kendall_tau(&a, &b);\n540\t        assert!((tau - 0.8).abs() < 0.01);\n541\t    }\n542\t\n543\t    #[test]\n544\t    fn test_jaccard_identical() {\n545\t        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n546\t        let b = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n547\t        assert!((jaccard_similarity(&a, &b) - 1.0).abs() < 0.001);\n548\t    }\n549\t\n550\t    #[test]\n551\t    fn test_jaccard_no_overlap() {\n552\t        let a = vec![1, 2, 3];\n553\t        let b = vec![4, 5, 6];\n554\t        assert!((jaccard_similarity(&a, &b) - 0.0).abs() < 0.001);\n555\t    }\n556\t\n557\t    #[test]\n558\t    fn test_jaccard_half_overlap() {\n559\t        let a assert!((jaccard_similarity(&a, &b) - 1.0 / 3.0).abs() < 0.001);\n564\t    }\n565\t\n566\t    #[test]\n567\t    fn test_skewed_distribution_sum() {\n568\t        let counts = generate_skewed_distribution(10000, 10, 10.0, &mut rand::thread_rng());\n569\t        let total: u64 = counts.iter().sum();\n570\t        assert!((total as i64 - 10000i64).abs() < 100); // Allow small rounding error\n571\t    }\n572\t\n573\t    #[test]\n574\t    fn test_skewed_distribution_has_skew() {\n575\t        let counts = generate_skewed_distribution(10000, 10, 100.0, &mut rand::thread_rng());\n576\t        let max = *counts.iter().max().unwrap();\n577\t        let min = *counts.iter().min().unwrap();\n578\t        // With skew factor 100, we expect significant imbalance.\n579\t        assert!(max > min * 10);\n580\t    }\n581\t\n582\t    #[test]\n583\t    fn test_simulation_runs() {\n584\t        let params = SimParams {\n585\t            total_docs: let result = simulate(&params);\n593\t        assert_eq!(result.query_results.len(), 10);\n594\t        assert!(result.aggregate.mean_kendall_tau >= -1.0);\n595\t        assert!(result.aggregate.mean_kendall_tau <= 1.0);\n596\t    }\n597\t}\n598\t"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"94d3f0a7-228d-43e2-a91f-e4b452f90587","uuid":"6da50e1d-1f70-4e1f-a855-100359ac3598","timestamp":"2026-05-09T05:18:35.631Z","tool_use_result":{"type":"text","file":{"filePath":"/home/coding/miroir/crates/miroir-core/src/score_comparability.rs","content":"//! Score comparability analysis: validates cross-shard ranking consistency.\n//!\n//! Implements Plan §15 OP#4: statistical validation that `_rankingScore`\n//! values remain comparable across shards with very different document-count\n//! distributions. Uses Kendall Tau correlation to measure ranking similarity\n//! between sharded and ground-truth (single-index) result orderings.\n\nuse serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};\n\n/// Parameters for a score comparability simulation run.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct SimParams {\n    /// Total number of documents in the corpus.\n    pub total_docs: u64,\n\n    /// Number of shards to distribute documents across.\n    pub shard_count: u32,\n\n    /// Skew factor: multiplier for document distribution imbalance.\n    /// 1.0 = uniform distribution. Higher values create more extreme skew.\n    /// Example: 100.0 means one shard gets 100× the median count.\n    pub skew_factor: f64,\n\n    /// Number of queries to run against the corpus.\n    pub num_queries: usize,\n\n    /// Number of top results to compare per query (K).\n    pub top_k: usize,\n\n    /// Random seed for reproducibility.\n    pub seed: u64,\n}\n\n/// Result of a single query comparison.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct QueryResult {\n    /// Query identifier.\n    pub query_id: usize,\n\n    /// Number of hits returned by ground truth (single-index).\n    pub ground_truth_hits: usize,\n\n    /// Number of hits returned by sharded execution.\n    pub sharded_hits: usize,\n\n    /// Kendall Tau correlation between result orderings.\n    pub kendall_tau: f64,\n\n    /// Jaccard similarity of the top-K result sets (ignoring order).\n    pub jaccard_similarity: f64,\n\n    /// Position of the first divergent result (0 if identical, top_k+1 if completely different).\n    pub first_divergence_position: usize,\n\n    /// Score statistics per shard.\n    pub shard_score_stats: Vec<ShardScoreStats>,\n}\n\n/// Score statistics for a single shard on a single query.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct ShardScoreStats {\n    /// Shard identifier.\n    pub shard_id: u32,\n\n    /// Number of documents on this shard.\n    pub doc_count: u64,\n\n    /// Number of hits returned by this shard.\n    pub hit_count: usize,\n\n    /// Minimum score returned.\n    pub min_score: f64,\n\n    /// Maximum score returned.\n    pub max_score: f64,\n\n    /// Mean score of returned hits.\n    pub mean_score: f64,\n\n    /// Score range (max - min).\n    pub score_range: f64,\n}\n\n/// Aggregate results across all queries.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct AggregateResult {\n    /// Mean Kendall Tau across all queries.\n    pub mean_kendall_tau: f64,\n\n    /// Standard deviation of Kendall Tau.\n    pub std_kendall_tau: f64,\n\n    /// Minimum Kendall Tau observed.\n    pub min_kendall_tau: f64,\n\n    /// Maximum Kendall Tau observed.\n    pub max_kendall_tau: f64,\n\n    /// Percentage of queries with τ ≥ 0.95.\n    pub percent_above_threshold: f64,\n\n    /// Mean Jaccard similarity.\n    pub mean_jaccard: f64,\n\n    /// Mean first divergence position.\n    pub mean_first_divergence: usize,\n\n    /// Shard population statistics (CV of document counts).\n    pub shard_pop_cv: f64,\n\n    /// Shard population ratio (max/median).\n    pub shard_pop_ratio: f64,\n}\n\n/// Simulated score comparability test result.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct SimResult {\n    pub params: SimParams,\n    pub aggregate: AggregateResult,\n    pub query_results: Vec<QueryResult>,\n    pub shard_doc_counts: Vec<u64>,\n}\n\n/// Run a score comparability simulation.\n///\n/// This models a simplified ranking system where:\n/// - Documents have relevance scores based on term frequency\n/// - Shards compute scores locally using their own document statistics\n/// - A ground-truth single-index uses global statistics\n///\n/// The simulation measures how well the sharded ordering matches the\n/// ground-truth ordering using Kendall Tau correlation.\npub fn simulate(params: &SimParams) -> SimResult {\n    use rand::rngs::StdRng;\n    use rand::SeedableRng;\n\n    let mut rng = StdRng::seed_from_u64(params.seed);\n\n    // Generate document distribution across shards with specified skew.\n    let shard_doc_counts = generate_skewed_distribution(\n        params.total_docs,\n        params.shard_count,\n        params.skew_factor,\n        &mut rng,\n    );\n\n    // Compute shard population statistics.\n    let total_docs = shard_doc_counts.iter().sum::<u64>() as f64;\n    let mean_docs = total_docs / params.shard_count as f64;\n    let variance = shard_doc_counts\n        .iter()\n        .map(|&c| (c as f64 - mean_docs).powi(2))\n        .sum::<f64>()\n        / params.shard_count as f64;\n    let cv = variance.sqrt() / mean_docs;\n    let median_docs = median(&shard_doc_counts);\n    let max_docs = *shard_doc_counts.iter().max().unwrap_or(&1) as f64;\n    let pop_ratio = max_docs / median_docs;\n\n    // Run queries and collect results.\n    let mut query_results = Vec::with_capacity(params.num_queries);\n\n    for qid in 0..params.num_queries {\n        let result = run_query(qid, params, &shard_doc_counts, &mut rng);\n        query_results.push(result);\n    }\n\n    // Compute aggregate statistics.\n    let taus: Vec<f64> = query_results.iter().map(|r| r.kendall_tau).collect();\n    let mean_tau = mean(&taus);\n    let std_tau = std_dev(&taus, mean_tau);\n    let min_tau = taus.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::min).unwrap_or(0.0);\n    let max_tau = taus.iter().cloned().reduce(f64::max).unwrap_or(0.0);\n    let above_threshold =\n        taus.iter().filter(|&&t| t >= 0.95).count() as f64 / taus.len() as f64 * 100.0;\n\n    let jaccards: Vec<f64> = query_results.iter().map(|r| r.jaccard_similarity).collect();\n    let mean_jaccard = mean(&jaccards);\n\n    let divergences: Vec<usize> = query_results\n        .iter()\n        .map(|r| r.first_divergence_position)\n        .collect();\n    let mean_divergence = mean_usize(&divergences);\n\n    let aggregate = AggregateResult {\n        mean_kendall_tau: mean_tau,\n        std_kendall_tau: std_tau,\n        min_kendall_tau: min_tau,\n        max_kendall_tau: max_tau,\n        percent_above_threshold: above_threshold,\n        mean_jaccard,\n        mean_first_divergence: mean_divergence,\n        shard_pop_cv: cv,\n        shard_pop_ratio: pop_ratio,\n    };\n\n    SimResult {\n        params: params.clone(),\n        aggregate,\n        query_results,\n        shard_doc_counts,\n    }\n}\n\n/// Generate a skewed document distribution across shards.\n///\n/// Uses a Pareto-like distribution to create realistic skew where\n/// a few shards have many more documents than others.\nfn generate_skewed_distribution(\n    total_docs: u64,\n    shard_count: u32,\n    skew_factor: f64,\n    rng: &mut impl rand::Rng,\n) -> Vec<u64> {\n    // Start with uniform weights.\n    let mut weights: Vec<f64> = (0..shard_count).map(|_| 1.0).collect();\n\n    // Apply skew: scale a few shards by the skew factor.\n    // For skew_factor = 100, scale the top 5% of shards.\n    let num_skewed = (shard_count as f64 / 20.0).ceil() as usize; // Top 5%\n    for i in 0..num_skewed.min(weights.len()) {\n        weights[i] *= skew_factor;\n    }\n\n    // Add some randomness to make it more realistic.\n    for w in &mut weights {\n        *w *= rng.gen_range(0.5..1.5);\n    }\n\n    // Normalize weights to sum to total_docs.\n    let weight_sum: f64 = weights.iter().sum();\n    let scale = total_docs as f64 / weight_sum;\n\n    weights\n        .into_iter()\n        .map(|w| (w * scale).max(1.0) as u64) // Ensure at least 1 doc per shard\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Run a single query and compare sharded vs ground-truth results.\nfn run_query(\n    query_id: usize,\n    params: &SimParams,\n    shard_doc_counts: &[u64],\n    rng: &mut impl rand::Rng,\n) -> QueryResult {\n    // Simulate a query by generating random relevance scores for documents.\n    // In a real system, scores would be based on term frequency, IDF, etc.\n    // Here we simulate the key effect: smaller shards tend to produce higher\n    // scores for the same documents because their local statistics are different.\n\n    let total_docs = params.total_docs as usize;\n\n    // Generate ground-truth scores (global IDF).\n    // Each document gets a base relevance score + some noise.\n    let mut ground_truth_scores: Vec<(usize, f64)> = (0..total_docs)\n        .map(|doc_id| {\n            let base_relevance = rng.gen::<f64>(); // Simulated term matching\n            let global_idf = 1.0; // Global IDF is uniform\n            let score = base_relevance * global_idf;\n            (doc_id, score)\n        })\n        .collect();\n\n    // Sort by score descending and take top-K.\n    ground_truth_scores.sort_by(|a, b| b.1.partial_cmp(&a.1).unwrap());\n\n    let ground_truth_top: Vec<usize> = ground_truth_scores\n        .iter()\n        .take(params.top_k)\n        .map(|(id, _)| *id)\n        .collect();\n\n    // Generate sharded scores (local IDF per shard).\n    // Key insight: local IDF is computed from shard-specific document counts.\n    // Smaller shards have fewer docs, so their IDF tends to be higher for\n    // the same term, leading to score inflation.\n\n    let mut sharded_scores: Vec<(usize, f64)> = Vec::new();\n\n    for (shard_id, &doc_count) in shard_doc_counts.iter().enumerate() {\n        let shard_id = shard_id as u32;\n        let doc_count_f64 = doc_count as f64;\n        let total_docs_f64 = params.total_docs as f64;\n\n        // Simulate local IDF effect: smaller shards → higher local IDF.\n        // In real BM25, IDF = log((N - df + 0.5) / (df + 0.5)) where N is doc count.\n        // We model this as: local_idf / global_idf ≈ log(N_global) / log(N_shard).\n        let global_idf_factor = (total_docs_f64 + 1.0).ln();\n        let local_idf_factor = (doc_count_f64 + 1.0).ln();\n        let idf_inflation = global_idf_factor / local_idf_factor.max(0.1);\n\n        // Documents on this shard get scores inflated by the local IDF factor.\n        let start_doc = shard_doc_counts[..shard_id as usize].iter().sum::<u64>() as usize;\n        let end_doc = start_doc + doc_count as usize;\n\n        for (doc_id, base_relevance) in ground_truth_scores\n            .iter()\n            .enumerate()\n            .skip(start_doc)\n            .take(end_doc.min(total_docs) - start_doc)\n        {\n            let score = base_relevance.1 * idf_inflation;\n            sharded_scores.push((doc_id, score));\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Sort sharded scores and take top-K.\n    sharded_scores.sort_by(|a, b| b.1.partial_cmp(&a.1).unwrap());\n\n    let sharded_top: Vec<usize> = sharded_scores\n        .iter()\n        .take(params.top_k)\n        .map(|(id, _)| *id)\n        .collect();\n\n    // Compute Kendall Tau between the two orderings.\n    let kendall_tau = kendall_tau(&ground_truth_top, &sharded_top);\n\n    // Compute Jaccard similarity (set overlap, ignoring order).\n    let jaccard = jaccard_similarity(&ground_truth_top, &sharded_top);\n\n    // Find first divergence position.\n    let first_divergence = ground_truth_top\n        .iter()\n        .zip(sharded_top.iter())\n        .position(|(a, b)| a != b)\n        .unwrap_or(params.top_k);\n\n    // Collect per-shard score statistics.\n    let shard_stats =\n        collect_shard_stats(query_id, shard_doc_counts, &sharded_scores, params.top_k);\n\n    QueryResult {\n        query_id,\n        ground_truth_hits: ground_truth_top.len(),\n        sharded_hits: sharded_top.len(),\n        kendall_tau,\n        jaccard_similarity: jaccard,\n        first_divergence_position: first_divergence,\n        shard_score_stats: shard_stats,\n    }\n}\n\n/// Collect score statistics for each shard.\nfn collect_shard_stats(\n    _query_id: usize,\n    shard_doc_counts: &[u64],\n    sharded_scores: &[(usize, f64)],\n    top_k: usize,\n) -> Vec<ShardScoreStats> {\n    let mut stats = Vec::new();\n\n    // Map doc_id back to its shard.\n    for (shard_idx, &doc_count) in shard_doc_counts.iter().enumerate() {\n        let shard_id = shard_idx as u32;\n        let start_doc = shard_doc_counts[..shard_idx].iter().sum::<u64>() as usize;\n        let end_doc = start_doc + doc_count as usize;\n\n        // Find scores from this shard in the top-K results.\n        let shard_hits: Vec<f64> = sharded_scores\n            .iter()\n            .take(top_k)\n            .filter(|(doc_id, _)| *doc_id >= start_doc && *doc_id < end_doc)\n            .map(|(_, score)| *score)\n            .collect();\n\n        if shard_hits.is_empty() {\n            continue;\n        }\n\n        let min_score = shard_hits.iter().fold(f64::INFINITY, |a, &b| a.min(b));\n        let max_score = shard_hits.iter().fold(f64::NEG_INFINITY, |a, &b| a.max(b));\n        let mean_score = shard_hits.iter().sum::<f64>() / shard_hits.len() as f64;\n\n        stats.push(ShardScoreStats {\n            shard_id,\n            doc_count,\n            hit_count: shard_hits.len(),\n            min_score,\n            max_score,\n            mean_score,\n            score_range: max_score - min_score,\n        });\n    }\n\n    stats\n}\n\n/// Compute Kendall Tau correlation between two ranked lists.\n///\n/// Returns a value in [-1, 1] where:\n/// - 1.0 = identical rankings\n/// - 0.0 = no correlation\n/// - -1.0 = completely inverted rankings\n///\n/// Uses the O(n²) algorithm which is fine for small K (typically ≤ 100).\nfn kendall_tau<T: Eq + std::hash::Hash + std::fmt::Debug>(rank1: &[T], rank2: &[T]) -> f64 {\n    if rank1.is_empty() || rank2.is_empty() {\n        return 1.0;\n    }\n\n    // Create position maps.\n    let pos1: std::collections::HashMap<&T, usize> = rank1\n        .iter()\n        .enumerate()\n        .map(|(i, item)| (item, i))\n        .collect();\n    let pos2: std::collections::HashMap<&T, usize> = rank2\n        .iter()\n        .enumerate()\n        .map(|(i, item)| (item, i))\n        .collect();\n\n    // Collect all unique items from both lists.\n    let all_items: std::collections::HashSet<&T> = rank1.iter().chain(rank2.iter()).collect();\n\n    // Count concordant and discordant pairs.\n    let mut concordant = 0;\n    let mut discordant = 0;\n\n    let items: Vec<&T> = all_items.into_iter().collect();\n    for i in 0..items.len() {\n        for j in (i + 1)..items.len() {\n            let a = items[i];\n            let b = items[j];\n\n            let pos1_a = pos1.get(a);\n            let pos1_b = pos1.get(b);\n            let pos2_a = pos2.get(a);\n            let pos2_b = pos2.get(b);\n\n            // A pair is only counted if both items appear in both lists.\n            let (p1a, p1b, p2a, p2b) = match (pos1_a, pos1_b, pos2_a, pos2_b) {\n                (Some(&x), Some(&y), Some(&u), Some(&v)) => (x, y, u, v),\n                _ => continue,\n            };\n\n            if (p1a < p1b && p2a < p2b) || (p1a > p1b && p2a > p2b) {\n                concordant += 1;\n            } else if (p1a < p1b && p2a > p2b) || (p1a > p1b && p2a < p2b) {\n                discordant += 1;\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    let total = concordant + discordant;\n    if total == 0 {\n        return 1.0;\n    }\n\n    (concordant - discordant) as f64 / total as f64\n}\n\n/// Compute Jaccard similarity between two sets (ignoring order).\nfn jaccard_similarity<T: Eq + std::hash::Hash>(set1: &[T], set2: &[T]) -> f64 {\n    let set1_hash: std::collections::HashSet<&T> = set1.iter().collect();\n    let set2_hash: std::collections::HashSet<&T> = set2.iter().collect();\n\n    let intersection = set1_hash.intersection(&set2_hash).count();\n    let union = set1_hash.union(&set2_hash).count();\n\n    if union == 0 {\n        return 1.0;\n    }\n\n    intersection as f64 / union as f64\n}\n\n/// Compute mean of a slice of floats.\nfn mean(values: &[f64]) -> f64 {\n    if values.is_empty() {\n        return 0.0;\n    }\n    values.iter().sum::<f64>() / values.len() as f64\n}\n\n/// Compute standard deviation of a slice of floats.\nfn std_dev(values: &[f64], mean_val: f64) -> f64 {\n    if values.len() <= 1 {\n        return 0.0;\n    }\n    let variance =\n        values.iter().map(|v| (v - mean_val).powi(2)).sum::<f64>() / (values.len() - 1) as f64;\n    variance.sqrt()\n}\n\n/// Compute mean of a slice of usize.\nfn mean_usize(values: &[usize]) -> usize {\n    if values.is_empty() {\n        return 0;\n    }\n    values.iter().sum::<usize>() / values.len()\n}\n\n/// Compute median of a slice of u64.\nfn median(values: &[u64]) -> f64 {\n    if values.is_empty() {\n        return 0.0;\n    }\n    let mut sorted = values.to_vec();\n    sorted.sort();\n    let len = sorted.len();\n    if len % 2 == 0 {\n        (sorted[len / 2 - 1] + sorted[len / 2]) as f64 / 2.0\n    } else {\n        sorted[len / 2] as f64\n    }\n}\n\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n// Tests\n// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_kendall_tau_identical() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        let b = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        assert!((kendall_tau(&a, &b) - 1.0).abs() < 0.001);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_kendall_tau_reversed() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        let b = vec![5, 4, 3, 2, 1];\n        assert!((kendall_tau(&a, &b) - (-1.0)).abs() < 0.001);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_kendall_tau_partial_overlap() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        let b = vec![1, 3, 2, 4, 5]; // Only 2 and 3 are swapped\n                                     // One discordant pair (2,3) out of 10 total: tau = (9 - 1) / 10 = 0.8\n        let tau = kendall_tau(&a, &b);\n        assert!((tau - 0.8).abs() < 0.01);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_jaccard_identical() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        let b = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        assert!((jaccard_similarity(&a, &b) - 1.0).abs() < 0.001);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_jaccard_no_overlap() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3];\n        let b = vec![4, 5, 6];\n        assert!((jaccard_similarity(&a, &b) - 0.0).abs() < 0.001);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_jaccard_half_overlap() {\n        let a = vec![1, 2, 3, 4];\n        let b = vec![3, 4, 5, 6];\n        // Intersection: {3, 4}, Union: {1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6}\n        // Jaccard = 2/6 = 1/3\n        assert!((jaccard_similarity(&a, &b) - 1.0 / 3.0).abs() < 0.001);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_skewed_distribution_sum() {\n        let counts = generate_skewed_distribution(10000, 10, 10.0, &mut rand::thread_rng());\n        let total: u64 = counts.iter().sum();\n        assert!((total as i64 - 10000i64).abs() < 100); // Allow small rounding error\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_skewed_distribution_has_skew() {\n        let counts = generate_skewed_distribution(10000, 10, 100.0, &mut rand::thread_rng());\n        let max = *counts.iter().max().unwrap();\n        let min = *counts.iter().min().unwrap();\n        // With skew factor 100, we expect significant imbalance.\n        assert!(max > min * 10);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_simulation_runs() {\n        let params = SimParams {\n            total_docs: 1000,\n            shard_count: 4,\n            skew_factor: 10.0,\n            num_queries: 10,\n            top_k: 10,\n            seed: 42,\n        };\n        let result = simulate(&params);\n        assert_eq!(result.query_results.len(), 10);\n        assert!(result.aggregate.mean_kendall_tau >= -1.0);\n        assert!(result.aggregate.mean_kendall_tau <= 1.0);\n    }\n}\n","numLines":598,"startLine":1,"totalLines":598}}}

Rendezvous hash-based routing and shard assignment.\n\nuse crate::topology::{Group, NodeId, Topology};\nuse std::hash::{Hash, Hasher};\nuse twox_hash::XxHash64;\n\n/// Compute a rendezvous score for a shard+node pair.\n///\n/// Higher scores win; used for deterministic shard assignment.\npub fn score(shard_id: u32, node_id: &str) -> u64 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    shard_id.hash(&mut h);\n    node_id.hash(&mut h);\n    h.finish()\n}\n\n/// Assign a shard to `rf` nodes within a single replica group.\n///\n/// `group_nodes` is the subset of nodes belonging to that group.\npub fn assign_shard_in_group(shard_id: u32, group_nodes: &[NodeId], rf: usize) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    let mut scored: Vec<(u64, &NodeId)> = group_nodes\n        .iter()\n        .map(|n| (score(shard_id, n.as_str()), n))\n        .collect();\n    scored.sort_unstable_by(|a, b| b.0.cmp(&a.0));\n    scored\n        .into_iter()\n        .take(rf)\n        .map(|(_, n)| n.clone())\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// All write targets for a document: the RF nodes in EACH replica group.\npub fn write_targets(shard_id: u32, topology: &Topology) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    topology\n        .groups()\n        .flat_map(|group| assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), topology.rf()))\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Select the replica group for a query (round-robin by query counter).\npub fn query_group(query_seq: u64, replica_groups: u32) -> u32 {\n    (query_seq % replica_groups as u64) as u32\n}\n\n/// The covering set for a search: one node per shard within the chosen group.\npub fn covering_set(shard_count: u32, group: &Group, rf: usize, query_seq: u64) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    (0..shard_count)\n        .map(|shard_id| {\n            let replicas = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), rf);\n            // rotate through replicas for intra-group load balancing\n            replicas[(query_seq as usize) % replicas.len()].clone()\n        })\n        .collect::<std::collections::HashSet<_>>()\n        .into_iter()\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Compute the shard ID for a document's primary key.\npub fn shard_for_key(primary_key: &str, shard_count: u32) -> u32 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    primary_key.hash(&mut h);\n    (h.finish() % shard_count as u64) as      *count >= 18 && *count <= 26,\n                \"Node shard count {} outside expected range [18, 26]\",\n                count\n            );\n        }\n\n        // Total should equal shard_count\n        let total: usize = node_shard_counts.values().sum();\n        assert_eq!(total, shard_count);\n    }\n\n    // Test 6: Top-RF placement changes minimally on add/remove\n    #[test]\n    fn test_top_rf_stability() {\n        let nodes_3 = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"];\n        let nodes_4 = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\", \"node4\"];\n        let rf = 2;\n        let shard_count = 100;\n\n        let mut changed_count = 0;\n        for shard_id in 0..shard_count {\n            let assign_3 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_3, rf);\n            let assign_4 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_4, rf);\n\n            // Count how many of the top-RF nodes changed\n            let set_3: std::collections::HashSet<_> = assign_3.iter().collect();\n            let set_4: std::collections::HashSet<_> = assign_4.iter().collect();\n\n            // A change is if the intersection is less than RF\n            let intersection = set_3.intersection(&set_4).count();\n            if intersection < rf {\n                changed_count += 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Minimal changes: at most ~30% should have completely different assignment\n        let max_expected = (shard_count as f64 * 0.3).ceil() as usize;\n        assert!(\n            changed_count <= max_expected,\n            \"Expected ≤ {} shards to change, but {} changed\",\n            max_expected,\n            changed_count\n        );\n    }\n\n    // Test 7: write_targets returns exactly RG × RF nodes\n    #[test]\n    fn test_query_group_distribution() {\n        let replica_groups = 3;\n        let queries = 1000;\n\n        let mut counts = vec![0; replica_groups as usize];\n        for seq in 0..queries {\n            let group = query_group(seq, replica_groups);\n            counts[group as usize] += 1;\n        }\n\n        // Each group should get roughly the same number of queries\n        let expected = Rendezvous hash-based routing and shard assignment.\n\nuse crate::topology::{Group, NodeId, Topology};\nuse std::hash::{Hash, Hasher};\nuse twox_hash::XxHash64;\n\n/// Compute a rendezvous score for a shard+node pair.\n///\n/// Higher scores win; used for deterministic shard assignment.\npub fn score(shard_id: u32, node_id: &str) -> u64 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    shard_id.hash(&mut h);\n    node_id.hash(&mut h);\n    h.finish()\n}\n\n/// Assign a shard to `rf` nodes within a single replica group.\n///\n/// `group_nodes` is the subset of nodes belonging to that group.\npub fn assign_shard_in_group(shard_id: u32, group_nodes: &[NodeId], rf: usize) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    let mut scored: Vec<(u64, &NodeId)> = group_nodes\n        .iter()\n        .map(|n| (score(shard_id, n.as_str()), n))\n        .collect();\n    scored.sort_unstable_by(|a, b| b.0.cmp(&a.0));\n    scored\n        .into_iter()\n        .take(rf)\n        .map(|(_, n)| n.clone())\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// All write targets for a document: the RF nodes in EACH replica group.\npub fn write_targets(shard_id: u32, topology: &Topology) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    topology\n        .groups()\n        .flat_map(|group| assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), topology.rf()))\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Select the replica group for a query (round-robin by query counter).\npub fn query_group(query_seq: u64, replica_groups: u32) -> u32 {\n    (query_seq % replica_groups as u64) as u32\n}\n\n/// The covering set for a search: one node per shard within the chosen group.\npub fn covering_set(shard_count: u32, group: &Group, rf: usize, query_seq: u64) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    (0..shard_count)\n        .map(|shard_id| {\n            let replicas = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), rf);\n            // rotate through replicas for intra-group load balancing\n            replicas[(query_seq as usize) % replicas.len()].clone()\n        })\n        .collect::<std::collections::HashSet<_>>()\n        .into_iter()\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Compute the shard ID for a document's primary key.\npub fn shard_for_key(primary_key: &str, shard_count: u32) -> u32 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    primary_key.hash(&mut h);\n    (h.finish() % shard_count as u64) as u32\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n &nodes, 1);\n\n        assert_eq!(assignment1, assignment2);\n    }\n\n    // Test 2: Score is stable across calls\n    #[test]\n    fn test_score_stability() {\n        let score1 = score(123, \"node1\");\n        let score2 = score(123, \"node1\");\n        assert_eq!(score1, score2);\n    }\n\n    // Test 3: Different shard+node pairs produce different scores\n    #[test]\n    fn test_score_uniqueness() {\n        let score1 = score(1, \"node1\");\n        let score2 = score(1, \"node2\");\n        let score3 = score(2, \"node1\");\n\n        assert_ne!(score1, score2);\n        assert_ne!(score1, score3);\n        assert_ne!(score2, score3);\n    }\n\n    // Test 4: Adding a 4th node moves at most ~2 × (1/4) of shards\n    #[test]\n    fn test_minimal_reshuffling_on_add() {\n        let nodes_3 = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"];\n        let nodes_4 = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\", \"node4\"];\n\n        let shard_count = 100;\n        let rf = 1;\n\n        let mut moved_count = 0;\n        for shard_id in 0..shard_count {\n            let assign_3 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_3, rf);\n            let assign_4 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_4, rf);\n\n            // Shard moved if its primary owner changed\n            if assign_3.first() != assign_4.first() {\n                moved_count += 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Expected: at most ~2 × (1/4) = 50% of shards\n        let max_expected = (shard_count as f64 * 0.5).ceil() as usize;\n        assert!(\n            moved_count <= max_expected,\n            \"Expected ≤ {} shards to move, but {} moved\",\n            max_expected,\n            moved_count\n        );\n    }\n\n    // Test 5: 64 shards / 3 nodes / RF=1 → each Rendezvous hash-based routing and shard assignment.\n\nuse crate::topology::{Group, NodeId, Topology};\nuse std::hash::{Hash, Hasher};\nuse twox_hash::XxHash64;\n\n/// Compute a rendezvous score for a shard+node pair.\n///\n/// Higher scores win; used for deterministic shard assignment.\npub fn score(shard_id: u32, node_id: &str) -> u64 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    shard_id.hash(&mut h);\n    node_id.hash(&mut h);\n    h.finish()\n}\n\n/// Assign a shard to `rf` nodes within a single replica group.\n///\n/// `group_nodes` is the subset of nodes belonging to that group.\npub fn assign_shard_in_group(shard_id: u32, group_nodes: &[NodeId], rf: usize) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    let mut scored: Vec<(u64, &NodeId)> = group_nodes\n        .iter()\n        .map(|n| (score(shard_id, n.as_str()), n))\n        .collect();\n    scored.sort_unstable_by(|a, b| b.0.cmp(&a.0));\n    scored\n        .into_iter()\n        .take(rf)\n        .map(|(_, n)| n.clone())\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// All write targets for a document: the RF nodes in EACH replica group.\npub fn write_targets(shard_id: u32, topology: &Topology) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    topology\n        .groups()\n        .flat_map(|group| assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), topology.rf()))\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Select the replica group for a query (round-robin by query counter).\npub fn query_group(query_seq: u64, replica_groups: u32) -> u32 {\n    (query_seq % replica_groups as u64) as u32\n}\n\n/// The covering set for a search: one node per shard within the chosen group.\npub fn covering_set(shard_count: u32, group: &Group, rf: usize, query_seq: u64) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    (0..shard_count)\n        .map(|shard_id| {\n            let replicas = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), rf);\n            // rotate through replicas for intra-group load balancing\n            replicas[(query_seq as usize) % replicas.len()].clone()\n        })\n        .collect::<std::collections::HashSet<_>>()\n        .into_iter()\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Compute the shard ID for a document's primary key.\npub fn shard_for_key(primary_key: &str, shard_count: u32) -> u32 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    primary_key.hash(&mut h);\n    (h.finish() % shard_count as u64) as u32\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use crate::topology::{Node, NodeId, NodeStatus};\n\n    // Test 1: Rendezvous assignment is deterministic given fixed node list\n    #[test]\n    fn test_rendezvous_determinism() {\n        let nodes: assignment1 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes, 1);\n        let assignment2 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes, 1);\n\n        assert_eq!(assignment1, assignment2);\n    }\n\n    // Test 2: Score is stable across calls\n    #[test]\n    fn test_score_stability() {\n        let score1 = score(123, \"node1\");\n        let score2 = score(123, \"node1\");\n        assert_eq!(score1, score2);\n    }\n\n    // Test 3: Different shard+node pairs produce different scores\n    #[test]\n    fn test_score_uniqueness() {\n        let score1 = score(1, \"node1\");\n        let score2 = score(1, \"node2\");\n        let score3 = score(2, \"node1\");\n\n        assert_ne!(score1, score2);\n        assert_ne!(score1, score3);\n        assert_ne!(score2, score3);\n    }\n\n    // Test 4: Adding a 4th node moves at most ~2 × (1/4) of shards\n    #[test]\n    fn test_minimal_reshuffling_on_add() {\n        let nodes_3 = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"];\n        let nodes_4 = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\", \"node4\"];\n\n        let shard_count = 100;\n        let rf = 1;\n\n        let mut moved_count = 0;\n        for shard_id in 0..shard_count {\n            let assign_3 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_3, rf);\n            let assign_4 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_4, rf);\n\n            // Shard moved if its primary owner changed\n            if assign_3.first() != assign_4.first() {\n                moved_count += 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Expected: at most ~2 × (1/4) = 50% of shards\n        let max_expected = (shard_count as f64 * 0.5).ceil() as usize;\n        assert!(\n            moved_count <= max_expected,\n            \"Expected ≤ {} shards to move, but {} moved\",\n            max_expected,\n            moved_count\n        );\n    }\n\n    // Test 5: 64 shards / 3 nodes / RF=1 → each node holds 18–26 shards\n    #[test]\n    fn test_shard_distribution_64_3_rf1() {\n        let nodes = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"];\n        let shard_count = 64;\n        let rf = 1;\n\n        let mut node_shard_counts: std::collections::HashMap<&str, usize> =\n            std::collections::HashMap::new();\n\n        for shard_id in 0..shard_count {\n            let assignment = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes, rf);\n            if let Some(node) = assignment.first() {\n                *node_shard_counts.entry(node).or_insert(0) += 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        for count in node_shard_counts.values() {\n            assert!(\n                *count >= 18 && *count <= 26,\n                \"Node shard count {} outside expected range [18, 26]\",\n                count\n            );\n        }\n\n        // Total should equal shard_count\n        let total: usize = node_shard_counts.values().sum();\n        assert_eq!(total, shard_count);\n    }\n\n    // Test 6: Top-RF placement changes minimally on add/remove\n    #[test]\n    fn test_top_rf_stability() {\n        let nodes_3 = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"];\n        let nodes_4 = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\", \"node4\"];\n        let rf = 2;\n        let shard_count = 100;\n\n        let mut changed_count = 0;\n        for shard_id in 0..shard_count {\n            let assign_3 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_3, rf);\n            let assign_4 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_4, rf);\n\n            // Count how many of the top-RF nodes changed\n            let set_3: std::collections::HashSet<_> = assign_3.iter().collect();\n            let set_4: std::collections::HashSet<_> = assign_4.iter().collect();\n\n            // A change is if the intersection is less than RF\n            let intersection = set_3.intersection(&set_4).count();\n            if intersection < rf {\n                changed_count += 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Minimal changes: at most ~30% should        }\n    }\n\n    // Test 10: covering_set handles intra-group replica rotation\n    #[test]\n    fn test_covering_set_replica_rotation() {\n        let mut topology = Topology::new(2); // RF=2\n        let group_id = 0;\n\n        // Add 3 nodes to a single group\n        for node_idx in 0..3 {\n            let node = Node::new(\n                NodeId::new(format!(\"node-{}\", node_idx)),\n         );\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Test 11: shard_for_key is deterministic\n    #[test]\n    fn test_shard_for_key_determinism() {\n        let key = \"user:12345\";\n        let shard_count = }\n\n    // Test 12: shard_for_key distributes keys evenly\n    #[test]\n    fn test_shard_for_key_distribution() {\n        let shard_count = 64;\n        let keys = 1000;\n\n        let mut counts = vec![0; shard_count as usize];\n        for i in 0..keys {\n            let key = format!(\"user:{}\", i);\n            let shard = shard_for_key(&key, shard_count);\n            counts[shard as usize] += 1;\n        }\n\n        // Each shard should get roughly keys / shard_count entries\n        let expected = keys / shard_count as usize;\n        for count in counts {\n            // Allow Rendezvous hash-based routing and shard assignment.\n\nuse crate::topology::{Group, NodeId, Topology};\nuse std::hash::{Hash, Hasher};\nuse twox_hash::XxHash64;\n\n/// Compute a rendezvous score for a shard+node pair.\n///\n/// Higher scores win; used for deterministic shard assignment.\npub fn score(shard_id: u32, node_id: &str) -> u64 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    shard_id.hash(&mut h);\n    node_id.hash(&mut h);\n    h.finish()\n}\n\n/// Assign a shard to `rf` nodes within a single replica group.\n///\n/// `group_nodes` is the subset of nodes belonging to that group.\npub fn assign_shard_in_group(shard_id: u32, group_nodes: &[NodeId], rf: usize) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    let mut scored: Vec<(u64, &NodeId)> = group_nodes\n        .iter()\n        .map(|n| (score(shard_id, n.as_str()), n))\n        .collect();\n    scored.sort_unstable_by(|a, b| b.0.cmp(&a.0));\n    scored\n        .into_iter()\n        .take(rf)\n        .map(|(_, n)| n.clone())\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// All write targets for a document: the RF nodes in EACH replica group.\npub fn write_targets(shard_id: u32, topology: &Topology) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    topology\n        .groups()\n        .flat_map(|group| assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), topology.rf()))\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Select the replica group for a query (round-robin by query counter).\npub fn query_group(query_seq: u64, replica_groups: u32) -> u32 {\n    (query_seq % replica_groups as u64) as u32\n}\n\n/// The covering set for a search: one node per shard within the chosen group.\npub fn covering_set(shard_count: u32, group: &Group, rf: usize, query_seq: u64) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    (0..shard_count)\n        .map(|shard_id| {\n            let replicas = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), rf);\n            // rotate through replicas for intra-group load balancing\n            replicas[(query_seq as usize) % replicas.len()].clone()\n        })\n        .collect::<std::collections::HashSet<_>>()\n        .into_iter()\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Compute the shard ID for a document's primary key.\npub fn shard_for_key(primary_key: &str, shard_count: u32) -> u32 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    primary_key.hash(&mut h);\n    (h.finish() % shard_count as u64) as u32\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use crate::topology::{Node, NodeId, NodeStatus};\n\n    // Test 1: Rendezvous assignment is deterministic given fixed node list\n    #[test]\n    fn test_rendezvous_determinism() {\n        let nodes: Vec<NodeId> = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"]\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|s| NodeId::new(s.to_string()))\n            .collect();\n        let shard_id = 42;\n\n        let assignment1 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes, 1);\n        let assignment2 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes, 1);\n\n        assert_eq!(assignment1, assignment2);\n    }\n\n    // Test 2: Score is stable across calls\n    #[test]\n    fn test_score_stability() {\n        let score1 = score(123, \"node1\");\n        let score2 = score(123, \"node1\");\n        assert_eq!(score1, score2);\n    }\n\n    // Test 3: Different shard+node pairs produce different scores\n    #[test]\n    fn test_score_uniqueness() {\n        let score1 = score(1, \"node1\");\n        let score2 = score(1, \"node2\");\n        let score3 = score(2, \"node1\");\n\n        assert_ne!(score1, score2);\n        assert_ne!(score1, score3);\n        assert_ne!(score2, score3);\n    }\n\n    // Test 4: Adding a 4th node moves at most ~2 × (1/4) of shards\n    #[test]\n    fn test_minimal_reshuffling_on_add() {\n        let nodes_3: Vec<NodeId> = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"]\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|s| NodeId::new(s.to_string()))\n            .collect();\n        let nodes_4: Vec<NodeId> = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\", \"node4\"]\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|s| NodeId::new(s.to_string()))\n            .collect();\n\n        let shard_count = 100;\n        let rf = 1;\n\n        let mut moved_count = 0;\n        for shard_id in 0..shard_count {\n            let assign_3 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_3, rf);\n            let assign_4 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_4, rf);\n\n            // Shard moved if its primary owner changed\n            if assign_3.first() != assign_4.first() {\n                moved_count += 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Expected: at most ~2 × (1/4) = 50% of shards\n        let max_expected = (shard_count as f64 * 0.5).ceil() as usize;\n        assert!(\n            moved_count <= max_expected,\n            \"Expected ≤ {} shards to move, but {} moved\",\n            max_expected,\n            moved_count\n        );\n    }\n\n    // Test 5: 64 shards / 3 nodes / RF=1 → each node holds 18–26 shards\n    #[test]\n    fn test_shard_distribution_64_3_rf1() {\n        let nodes = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"];\n        let shard_count = 64;\n        let rf = 1;\n\n        let mut node_shard_counts: std::collections::HashMap<&str, usize> =\n            std::collections::HashMap::new();\n\n        for shard_id in 0..shard_count {\n            let assignment = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes, rf);\n            if let Some(node) = assignment.first() {\n                *node_shard_counts.entry(node).or_insert(0) += 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        for count in node_shard_counts.values() {\n            assert!(\n                *count >= 18 && *count <= 26,\n                \"Node shard count {} outside expected range [18, 26]\",\n                count\n            );\n        }\n\n        // Total should equal shard_count\n        let total: usize = node_shard_counts.values().sum();\n        assert_eq!(total, shard_count);\n    }\n\n    // Test 6: Top-RF placement changes minimally on add/remove\n    #[test]\n    fn test_top_rf_stability() {\n        let nodes_3 = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"];\n        let nodes_4 = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\", \"node4\"];\n        let rf = 2;\n        let shard_count = 100;\n\n        let mut changed_count = 0;\n        for shard_id in 0..shard_count {\n            let assign_3 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_3, rf);\n            let assign_4 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_4, rf);\n\n            // Count how many of the top-RF nodes changed\n            let set_3: std::collections::HashSet<_> = assign_3.iter().collect();\n            let set_4: std::collections::HashSet<_> = assign_4.iter().collect();\n\n            // A change is if the intersection is less than RF\n            let intersection = set_3.intersection(&set_4).count();\n            if intersection < rf {\n                changed_count += 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Minimal changes: at most ~30% should have completely different assignment\n        let max_expected = (shard_count as f64 * 0.3).ceil() as usize;\n        assert!(\n            changed_count <= max_expected,\n            \"Expected ≤ {} shards to change, but {} changed\",\n            max_expected,\n            changed_count\n        );\n    }\n\n    // Test 7: write_targets returns exactly RG × RF nodes\n    #[test]\n    fn test_write_targets_count() {\n        let mut topology = Topology::new(2); // RF=2\n\n        // 3 replica groups, 2 nodes each\n        for group_id in 0..3 {\n            for node_idx in 0..2 {\n                let node = Node::new(\n                    NodeId::new(format!(\"node-g{}-{}\", group_id, node_idx)),\n                    format!(\"http://example.com/{}\", group_id),\n                    group_id,\n                );\n                topology.add_node(node);\n            }\n        }\n\n        let shard_id = 42;\n        let targets = write_targets(shard_id, &topology);\n\n        // Should be RG (3) × RF (2) = 6 nodes\n        assert_eq!(targets.len(), 6);\n\n        // All targets should be unique\n        let unique: std::collections::HashSet<_> = targets.iter().collect();\n        assert_eq!(unique.len(), 6);\n\n        // Each replica group should contribute exactly RF nodes\n        for group in topology.groups() {\n            let group_targets: Vec<_> = targets\n                .iter()\n                .filter(|t| group.nodes().contains(t))\n                .collect();\n            assert_eq!(\n                group_targets.len(),\n                topology.rf(),\n                \"Group {} should contribute exactly RF nodes\",\n                group.id\n            );\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Test 8: query_group distributes evenly\n    #[test]\n    fn test_query_group_distribution() {\n        let replica_groups = 3;\n        let queries = 1000;\n\n        let mut counts = vec![0; replica_groups as usize];\n        for seq in 0..queries {\n            let group = query_group(seq, replica_groups);\n            counts[group as usize] += 1;\n        }\n\n        // Each group should get roughly the same number of queries\n        let expected = queries / replica_groups as usize;\n        for count in counts {\n            assert!(\n                count >= expected - 1 && count <= expected + 1,\n                \"Group query count {} outside expected range [{}, {}]\",\n                count,\n                expected - 1,\n                expected + 1\n            );\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Test 9: covering_set returns exactly one node per shard\n    #[test]\n    fn test_covering_set_one_per_shard() {\n        let mut topology = Topology::new(2); // RF=2\n        let group_id = 0;\n        let num_nodes = 5;\n\n        // Add nodes to a single group\n        for node_idx in 0..num_nodes {\n            let node = Node::new(\n                NodeId::new(format!(\"node-{}\", node_idx)),\n                format!(\"http://example.com/{}\", node_idx),\n                group_id,\n            );\n            topology.add_node(node);\n        }\n\n        let group = topology.group(group_id).unwrap();\n        let shard_count = 64;\n        let rf = 2;\n        let query_seq = 0;\n\n        let covering = covering_set(shard_count, group, rf, query_seq);\n\n        // Should have exactly one node per shard\n        assert_eq!(covering.len(), shard_count as usize);\n\n        // All nodes should be from the group\n        for node in &covering {\n            assert!(group.nodes().contains(node));\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Test 10: covering_set handles intra-group replica rotation\n    #[test]\n    fn      \"Covering set should rotate replicas across queries\"\n            );\n        }\n    }\n\n    // Test 11: shard_for_key is deterministic\n    #[test]\n    fn test_shard_for_key_determinism() assert_eq!(shard1, shard2);\n        assert!(shard1 < shard_count);\n    }\n\n    // Test 12: shard_for_key distributes keys evenly\n    #[test]\n    fn test_shard_for_key_distribution() {\n Rendezvous hash-based routing and shard assignment.\n\nuse crate::topology::{Group, NodeId, Topology};\nuse std::hash::{Hash, Hasher};\nuse twox_hash::XxHash64;\n\n/// Compute a rendezvous score for a shard+node pair.\n///\n/// Higher scores win; used for deterministic shard assignment.\npub fn score(shard_id: u32, node_id: &str) -> u64 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    shard_id.hash(&mut h);\n    node_id.hash(&mut h);\n    h.finish()\n}\n\n/// Assign a shard to `rf` nodes within a single replica group.\n///\n/// `group_nodes` is the subset of nodes belonging to that group.\npub fn assign_shard_in_group(shard_id: u32, group_nodes: &[NodeId], rf: usize) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    let mut scored: Vec<(u64, &NodeId)> = group_nodes\n        .iter()\n        .map(|n| (score(shard_id, n.as_str()), n))\n        .collect();\n    scored.sort_unstable_by(|a, b| b.0.cmp(&a.0));\n    scored\n        .into_iter()\n        .take(rf)\n        .map(|(_, n)| n.clone())\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// All write targets for a document: the RF nodes in EACH replica group.\npub fn write_targets(shard_id: u32, topology: &Topology) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    topology\n        .groups()\n        .flat_map(|group| assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), topology.rf()))\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Select the replica group for a query (round-robin by query counter).\npub fn query_group(query_seq: u64, replica_groups: u32) -> u32 {\n    (query_seq % replica_groups as u64) as u32\n}\n\n/// The covering set for a search: one node per shard within the chosen group.\npub fn covering_set(shard_count: u32, group: &Group, rf: usize, query_seq: u64) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    (0..shard_count)\n        .map(|shard_id| {\n            let replicas = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), rf);\n            // rotate through replicas for intra-group load balancing\n            replicas[(query_seq as usize) % replicas.len()].clone()\n        })\n        .collect::<std::collections::HashSet<_>>()\n        .into_iter()\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Compute the shard ID for a document's primary key.\npub fn shard_for_key(primary_key: &str, shard_count: u32) -> u32 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    primary_key.hash(&mut h);\n    (h.finish() % shard_count as u64) as u32\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n Rendezvous hash-based routing and shard assignment.\n\nuse crate::topology::{Group, NodeId, Topology};\nuse std::hash::{Hash, Hasher};\nuse twox_hash::XxHash64;\n\n/// Compute a rendezvous score for a shard+node pair.\n///\n/// Higher scores win; used for deterministic shard assignment.\npub fn score(shard_id: u32, node_id: &str) -> u64 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    shard_id.hash(&mut h);\n    node_id.hash(&mut h);\n    h.finish()\n}\n\n/// Assign a shard to `rf` nodes within a single replica group.\n///\n/// `group_nodes` is the subset of nodes belonging to that group.\npub fn assign_shard_in_group(shard_id: u32, group_nodes: &[NodeId], rf: usize) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    let mut scored: Vec<(u64, &NodeId)> = group_nodes\n        .iter()\n        .map(|n| (score(shard_id, n.as_str()), n))\n        .collect();\n    scored.sort_unstable_by(|a, b| b.0.cmp(&a.0));\n    scored\n        .into_iter()\n        .take(rf)\n        .map(|(_, n)| n.clone())\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// All write targets for a document: the RF nodes in EACH replica group.\npub fn write_targets(shard_id: u32, topology: &Topology) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    topology\n        .groups()\n        .flat_map(|group| assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), topology.rf()))\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Select the replica group for a query (round-robin by query counter).\npub fn query_group(query_seq: u64, replica_groups: u32) -> u32 {\n    (query_seq % replica_groups as u64) as u32\n}\n\n/// The covering set for a search: one node per shard within the chosen group.\npub fn covering_set(shard_count: u32, group: &Group, rf: usize, query_seq: u64) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    (0..shard_count)\n        .map(|shard_id| {\n            let replicas = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), rf);\n            // rotate through replicas for intra-group load balancing\n            replicas[(query_seq as usize) % replicas.len()].clone()\n        })\n        .collect::<std::collections::HashSet<_>>()\n        .into_iter()\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Compute the shard ID for a document's primary key.\npub fn shard_for_key(primary_key: &str, shard_count: u32) -> u32 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    primary_key.hash(&mut h);\n    (h.finish() % shard_count as u64) as u32\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n Rendezvous hash-based routing and shard assignment.\n\nuse crate::topology::{Group, NodeId, Topology};\nuse std::hash::{Hash, Hasher};\nuse twox_hash::XxHash64;\n\n/// Compute a rendezvous score for a shard+node pair.\n///\n/// Higher scores win; used for deterministic shard assignment.\npub fn score(shard_id: u32, node_id: &str) -> u64 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    shard_id.hash(&mut h);\n    node_id.hash(&mut h);\n    h.finish()\n}\n\n/// Assign a shard to `rf` nodes within a single replica group.\n///\n/// `group_nodes` is the subset of nodes belonging to that group.\npub fn assign_shard_in_group(shard_id: u32, group_nodes: &[NodeId], rf: usize) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    let mut scored: Vec<(u64, &NodeId)> = group_nodes\n        .iter()\n        .map(|n| (score(shard_id, n.as_str()), n))\n        .collect();\n    scored.sort_unstable_by(|a, b| b.0.cmp(&a.0));\n    scored\n        .into_iter()\n        .take(rf)\n        .map(|(_, n)| n.clone())\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// All write targets for a document: the RF nodes in EACH replica group.\npub fn write_targets(shard_id: u32, topology: &Topology) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    topology\n        .groups()\n        .flat_map(|group| assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), topology.rf()))\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Select the replica group for a query (round-robin by query counter).\npub fn query_group(query_seq: u64, replica_groups: u32) -> u32 {\n    (query_seq % replica_groups as u64) as u32\n}\n\n/// The covering set for a search: one node per shard within the chosen group.\npub fn covering_set(shard_count: u32, group: &Group, rf: usize, query_seq: u64) -> Vec<NodeId> {\n    (0..shard_count)\n        .map(|shard_id| {\n            let replicas = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, group.nodes(), rf);\n            // rotate through replicas for intra-group load balancing\n            replicas[(query_seq as usize) % replicas.len()].clone()\n        })\n        .collect::<std::collections::HashSet<_>>()\n        .into_iter()\n        .collect()\n}\n\n/// Compute the shard ID for a document's primary key.\npub fn shard_for_key(primary_key: &str, shard_count: u32) -> u32 {\n    let mut h = XxHash64::with_seed(0);\n    primary_key.hash(&mut h);\n    (h.finish() % shard_count as u64) as u32\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n    use crate::topology::{Node, NodeId, NodeStatus};\n\n    // Test 1: Rendezvous assignment is deterministic given fixed node list\n    #[test]\n    fn test_rendezvous_determinism() {\n        let nodes: Vec<NodeId> = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"]\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|s| NodeId::new(s.to_string()))\n            .collect();\n        let shard_id = 42;\n\n        let assignment1 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes, 1);\n        let assignment2 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes, 1);\n\n        assert_eq!(assignment1, assignment2);\n    }\n\n    // Test 2: Score is stable across calls\n    #[test]\n    fn test_score_stability() {\n        let score1 = score(123, \"node1\");\n        let score2 = score(123, \"node1\");\n        assert_eq!(score1, score2);\n    }\n\n    // Test 3: Different shard+node pairs produce different scores\n    #[test]\n    fn test_score_uniqueness() {\n        let score1 = score(1, \"node1\");\n        let score2 = score(1, \"node2\");\n        let score3 = score(2, \"node1\");\n\n        assert_ne!(score1, score2);\n        assert_ne!(score1, score3);\n        assert_ne!(score2, score3);\n    }\n\n    // Test 4: Adding a 4th node moves at most ~2 × (1/4) of shards\n    #[test]\n    fn test_minimal_reshuffling_on_add() {\n        let nodes_3: Vec<NodeId> = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"]\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|s| NodeId::new(s.to_string()))\n            .collect();\n        let nodes_4: Vec<NodeId> = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\", \"node4\"]\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|s| NodeId::new(s.to_string()))\n            .collect();\n\n        let shard_count = 100;\n        let rf = 1;\n\n        let mut moved_count = 0;\n        for shard_id in 0..shard_count {\n            let assign_3 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_3, rf);\n            let assign_4 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_4, rf);\n\n            // Shard moved if its primary owner changed\n            if assign_3.first() != assign_4.first() {\n                moved_count += 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        // Expected: at most ~2 × (1/4) = 50% of shards\n        let max_expected = (shard_count as f64 * 0.5).ceil() as usize;\n        assert!(\n            moved_count <= max_expected,\n            \"Expected ≤ {} shards to move, but {} moved\",\n            max_expected,\n            moved_count\n        );\n    }\n\n    // Test 5: 64 shards / 3 nodes / RF=1 → each node holds 18–26 shards\n    #[test]\n    fn test_shard_distribution_64_3_rf1() {\n        let nodes: Vec<NodeId> = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\"]\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|s| NodeId::new(s.to_string()))\n            .collect();\n        let shard_count = 64;\n        let rf = 1;\n\n        let mut node_shard_counts: std::collections::HashMap<String, usize> =\n            std::collections::HashMap::new();\n\n        for shard_id in 0..shard_count {\n            let assignment = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes, rf);\n            if let Some(node) = assignment.first() {\n                *node_shard_counts.entry(node.as_str().to_string()).or_insert(0) += 1;\n            }\n        }\n\n        for count in node_shard_counts.values() {\n            assert!(\n                *count >= .collect();\n        let nodes_4: Vec<NodeId> = vec![\"node1\", \"node2\", \"node3\", \"node4\"]\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|s| NodeId::new(s.to_string()))\n            .collect();\n        let rf = 2;\n        let shard_count = 100;\n\n        let mut changed_count = 0;\n        for shard_id in 0..shard_count {\n            let assign_3 = assign_shard_in_group(shard_id, &nodes_3, }\n\n    // Test 12: shard_for_key distributes keys evenly\n    #[test]\n    fn test_shard_for_key_distribution() {\n        let shard_count = 64;\n        let keys = 1000;\n\n        let mut counts =
